Currently pregnant at 28 weeks 6 days! I've been feel physically really well with good energy still and very little complaints. However this pregnancy has been very much more mental taxing for me. 9 weeks ago we went for out anatomy scan and were diagnosed with IUGR, or fetal growth restriction. We also found out then it's a girl which was our hope. At that time baby girl was measuring at the 5th percentile classifying the growth restriction as mild. We were then scheduled for follow up growth scans every 3 weeks and because she was so small at the first scan they weren't able to get a very good picture of her heart, they wanted to see us just one week later for another try. At that visit baby had made little to no progress growth wise tanking her into less than the 1st percentile and reclasifying the growth restriction as severe. I was then expected to follow up three times a week for a bio physical profile, to check on baby's overall health and an umbilical artery dopler to check blood flow from the placenta. It was then that we found an intermittent absence of flow in the artery. That's indicative of an insufficient placenta.  The blood flow got better, then worse, then better again, and then severely worse with a pertinent absence of flow at 25 weeks. I was admitted to the hospital and given corticosteroids. That's more baby's lung maturity and preventing brain bleeding if I were to deliver that early. Luckily for us it just so happened to improve bloodflow once again. I stayed in the hospital for a week and then was able to get home to the rest of my family. It has been a lot of long drives and watching and waiting. The doctors told me that expect to see the absence of flow again at some point. Even if they don't, given the history they will recommend delivery between 33 and 34 weeks. It certainly beats 25 but it means that baby will be headed for NICU. Things are looking good since the steroids no absence of flow so far at all and baby grew for less than the 1st to the second percentile. If she grow to above the 5th percentile by 33-34 weeks I can think about potentially a full term baby. That's what I'm hoping for.   The watching and waiting for things to decline is difficult. The term insufficient placenta is difficult. I feel somehow like it's my fault. And even knowing that it's not its difficult to know that my body isn't providing a safe place for this baby to grow. It's nothing compared to cancer, but I do have MS. I wasn't diagnosed until after my first baby was already 1, therfore I never took any treatment. For the past 3 years before this pregnancy I was taking immunosuppressing injections once a month. There is no research to support my assumptions, but none disprove them either.  My MS specialist doesn't think so. He thought it would be okay for take the entire 1st trimester. My maternal fetal specialists think that it's a possibility. It's difficult when your body fails you. It's even more more difficult when it fails your baby too. I'm thankful you guys don't need to go though this. There is comfort in knowing that I'm not alone but I wouldn't wish it on anyone. It's good to hear that your babe, and back are happy and healthy.    Does bec have a pregnancy pillow? They really help with hip pain stuff at bedtime

I am 6 months postpartum, and the worst part of being pregnant was the calf cramps!! I collaborated with my doctor and Endocrinologist (as I also have hyperthyroidism, which also increases my risk for said cramps), and we decided to have me take extra magnesium everyday until about 1 week postpartum as you do remain a lil stiff and swollen afterwards. It was a game changer. I went from waking up in the middle of the night screaming because nothing I did would make the cramps stop, to rarely getting them. Also, compression socks that go over your calves as well feel so refreshing. I definitely recommend them.

Reheating rice isn't the best idea esp for Bec. NEVER EVER MICROWAVE LEFTOVER RICE!!! It won't heat evenly.  The longer cooked rice is left at room temperature, the more likely it is that the bacteria or toxins could make the rice unsafe to eat.  Symptoms of food poisoning If you eat rice that contains Bacillus cereus bacteria, you may be sick and experience vomiting or diarrhoea about 1 to 5 hours afterwards. Symptoms are relatively mild and usually last about 24 hours.  Tips on serving rice safely Ideally, serve rice as soon as it has been cooked. If that is not possible, cool the rice as quickly as possible (ideally within 1 hour). Keep rice in the fridge for no more than 1 day until reheating. When you reheat rice, always check that it's steaming hot all the way through. Do not reheat rice more than once.
